---
title: "Functions and Operators"
old_description: "CockroachDB supports many built-in functions, aggregate functions, and operators."
---

CockroachDB supports the following SQL functions and operators for use in [scalar expressions](/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions).

<Tip>
In the [built-in SQL shell](/docs/v25.4/cockroach-sql#help), use `\hf [function]` to get inline help about a specific function.
</Tip>

## Special syntax forms

The following syntax forms are recognized for compatibility with the SQL standard and PostgreSQL, but are equivalent to regular built-in functions:

<table><thead><tr><th>Special form</th><th>Equivalent to</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>AT TIME ZONE</code></td><td><code>timezone()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;CATALOG</code></td><td><code>current&#95;catalog()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>COLLATION FOR</code></td><td><code>pg&#95;collation&#95;for()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;DATE</code></td><td><code>current&#95;date()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;ROLE</code></td><td><code>current&#95;user()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;SCHEMA</code></td><td><code>current&#95;schema()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;TIMESTAMP</code></td><td><code>current&#95;timestamp()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;TIME</code></td><td><code>current&#95;time()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>CURRENT&#95;USER</code></td><td><code>current&#95;user()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>EXTRACT(&lt;part&gt; FROM &lt;value&gt;)</code></td><td><code>extract("&lt;part&gt;", &lt;value&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>EXTRACT&#95;DURATION(&lt;part&gt; FROM &lt;value&gt;)</code></td><td><code>extract&#95;duration("&lt;part&gt;", &lt;value&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>OVERLAY(&lt;text1&gt; PLACING &lt;text2&gt; FROM &lt;int1&gt; FOR &lt;int2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>overlay(&lt;text1&gt;, &lt;text2&gt;, &lt;int1&gt;, &lt;int2&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>OVERLAY(&lt;text1&gt; PLACING &lt;text2&gt; FROM &lt;int&gt;)</code></td><td><code>overlay(&lt;text1&gt;, &lt;text2&gt;, &lt;int&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>POSITION(&lt;text1&gt; IN &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>strpos(&lt;text2&gt;, &lt;text1&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>SESSION&#95;USER</code></td><td><code>current&#95;user()</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>SUBSTRING(&lt;text&gt; FOR &lt;int1&gt; FROM &lt;int2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>substring(&lt;text&gt;, &lt;int2&gt;, &lt;int1&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>SUBSTRING(&lt;text&gt; FOR &lt;int&gt;)</code></td><td><code>substring(&lt;text&gt;, 1, &lt;int&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>SUBSTRING(&lt;text&gt; FROM &lt;int1&gt; FOR &lt;int2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>substring(&lt;text&gt;, &lt;int1&gt;, &lt;int2&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>SUBSTRING(&lt;text&gt; FROM &lt;int&gt;)</code></td><td><code>substring(&lt;text&gt;, &lt;int&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(&lt;text1&gt; FROM &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>btrim(&lt;text2&gt;, &lt;text1&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(&lt;text1&gt;, &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>btrim(&lt;text1&gt;, &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(FROM &lt;text&gt;)</code></td><td><code>btrim(&lt;text&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(LEADING &lt;text1&gt; FROM &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>ltrim(&lt;text2&gt;, &lt;text1&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(LEADING FROM &lt;text&gt;)</code></td><td><code>ltrim(&lt;text&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(TRAILING &lt;text1&gt; FROM &lt;text2&gt;)</code></td><td><code>rtrim(&lt;text2&gt;, &lt;text1&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>TRIM(TRAILING FROM &lt;text&gt;)</code></td><td><code>rtrim(&lt;text&gt;)</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>USER</code></td><td><code>current&#95;user()</code></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Function volatility

A function's *volatility* is a promise to the [optimizer](/docs/v25.4/cost-based-optimizer) about the behavior of the function.

<table><thead><tr><th>Type</th><th>Description</th><th>Examples</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Volatile</td><td>The function can modify the state of the database and is not guaranteed to return the same results given the same arguments in any context.</td><td><code>random</code>, <code>nextval</code>, <code>now</code></td></tr><tr><td>Stable</td><td>The function is guaranteed to return the same results given the same arguments whenever it is evaluated within the same statement. The optimizer can optimize multiple calls of the function to a single call.</td><td><code>current&#95;timestamp</code>, <code>current&#95;date</code></td></tr><tr><td>Immutable</td><td>The function does not depend on configuration settings and is guaranteed to return the same results given the same arguments in any context. The optimizer can pre-evaluate the function when a query calls it with constant arguments.</td><td><code>log</code>, <code>from&#95;json</code></td></tr><tr><td>Leakproof</td><td>The function does not depend on configuration settings and is guaranteed to return the same results given the same arguments in any context. In addition, no information about the arguments is conveyed except via the return value. Any function that might throw an error depending on the values of its arguments is not leakproof. Leakproof is strictly stronger than Immutable.</td><td>Integer <a href="#comparison-functions">comparison</a></td></tr></tbody></table>

## Conditional and function-like operators

The following table lists the operators that look like built-in functions but have special evaluation rules:

<table><thead><tr><th>Operator</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>ANNOTATE&#95;TYPE(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#explicitly-typed-expressions">Explicitly Typed Expression</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>ARRAY(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#conversion-of-subquery-results-to-an-array">Conversion of Subquery Results to An Array</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>ARRAY&#91;...&#93;</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#array-constructors">Conversion of Scalar Expressions to An Array</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>CAST(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#explicit-type-coercions">Type Cast</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>COALESCE(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#coalesce-and-ifnull-expressions">First non-NULL expression with Short Circuit</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>EXISTS(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#existence-test-on-the-result-of-subqueries">Existence Test on the Result of Subqueries</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>IF(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#if-expressions">Conditional Evaluation</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>IFNULL(...)</code></td><td>Alias for <code>COALESCE</code> restricted to two operands</td></tr><tr><td><code>NULLIF(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#nullif-expressions">Return <code>NULL</code> conditionally</a></td></tr><tr><td><code>ROW(...)</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#tuple-constructors">Tuple Constructor</a></td></tr></tbody></table>

## User-defined functions

In addition to the built-in functions described in the following sections, CockroachDB supports user-defined functions. For details, see [User-Defined Functions](/docs/v25.4/user-defined-functions).

## Built-in functions

### Array functions

### Cryptographic functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>crypt(password: string, salt: string) → string</code></td><td>Generates a hash based on a password and salt. The hash algorithm and number of rounds if applicable are encoded in the salt.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>decrypt(data: bytes, key: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Decrypt <code>data</code> with <code>key</code> using the cipher method specified by <code>type</code>.<br/><br/>The cipher type must have the format <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;&#91;-&lt;mode&gt;&#93;&#91;/pad:&lt;padding&gt;&#93;</code> where:<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;</code> is <code>aes</code><br/><br/>- <code>&lt;mode&gt;</code> is <code>cbc</code> (default)<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;padding&gt;</code> is <code>pkcs</code> (default) or <code>none</code><br/><br/>This function requires an enterprise license on a CCL distribution.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>decrypt&#95;iv(data: bytes, key: bytes, iv: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Decrypt <code>data</code> with <code>key</code> using the cipher method specified by <code>type</code>. If the mode is CBC, the provided <code>iv</code> will be used. Otherwise, it will be ignored.<br/><br/>The cipher type must have the format <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;&#91;-&lt;mode&gt;&#93;&#91;/pad:&lt;padding&gt;&#93;</code> where:<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;</code> is <code>aes</code><br/><br/>- <code>&lt;mode&gt;</code> is <code>cbc</code> (default)<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;padding&gt;</code> is <code>pkcs</code> (default) or <code>none</code><br/><br/>This function requires an enterprise license on a CCL distribution.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>digest(data: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Computes a binary hash of the given <code>data</code>. <code>type</code> is the algorithm to use (md5, sha1, sha224, sha256, sha384, or sha512).</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>digest(data: string, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Computes a binary hash of the given <code>data</code>. <code>type</code> is the algorithm to use (md5, sha1, sha224, sha256, sha384, or sha512).</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>encrypt(data: bytes, key: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Encrypt <code>data</code> with <code>key</code> using the cipher method specified by <code>type</code>.<br/><br/>The cipher type must have the format <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;&#91;-&lt;mode&gt;&#93;&#91;/pad:&lt;padding&gt;&#93;</code> where:<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;</code> is <code>aes</code><br/><br/>- <code>&lt;mode&gt;</code> is <code>cbc</code> (default)<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;padding&gt;</code> is <code>pkcs</code> (default) or <code>none</code><br/><br/>This function requires an enterprise license on a CCL distribution.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>encrypt&#95;iv(data: bytes, key: bytes, iv: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Encrypt <code>data</code> with <code>key</code> using the cipher method specified by <code>type</code>. If the mode is CBC, the provided <code>iv</code> will be used. Otherwise, it will be ignored.<br/><br/>The cipher type must have the format <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;&#91;-&lt;mode&gt;&#93;&#91;/pad:&lt;padding&gt;&#93;</code> where:<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;algorithm&gt;</code> is <code>aes</code><br/><br/>- <code>&lt;mode&gt;</code> is <code>cbc</code> (default)<br/><br/>- <code>&lt;padding&gt;</code> is <code>pkcs</code> (default) or <code>none</code><br/><br/>This function requires an enterprise license on a CCL distribution.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>gen&#95;random&#95;bytes(count: int) → bytes</code></td><td>Returns <code>count</code> cryptographically strong random bytes. At most 1024 bytes can be extracted at a time.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>gen&#95;salt(type: string) → string</code></td><td>Generates a salt for input into the <code>crypt</code> function using the default number of rounds.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>gen&#95;salt(type: string, iter&#95;count: int) → string</code></td><td>Generates a salt for input into the <code>crypt</code> function using <code>iter&#95;count</code> number of rounds.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>hmac(data: bytes, key: bytes, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Calculates hashed MAC for <code>data</code> with key <code>key</code>. <code>type</code> is the same as in <code>digest()</code>.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>hmac(data: string, key: string, type: string) → bytes</code></td><td>Calculates hashed MAC for <code>data</code> with key <code>key</code>. <code>type</code> is the same as in <code>digest()</code>.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr></tbody></table>

### DECIMAL functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>hlc&#95;to&#95;timestamp(hlc: decimal) → timestamptz</code></td><td>Returns a TimestampTZ representation of a CockroachDB HLC in decimal form.Note that a TimestampTZ has less precision than a CockroachDB HLC. It is intended as a convenience function to display HLCs in a print-friendly form. Use the decimal value if you rely on the HLC for accuracy.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr></tbody></table>

### Date and time functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>age(end: timestamptz, begin: timestamptz) → interval</code></td><td>Calculates the interval between <code>begin</code> and <code>end</code>, normalized into years, months and days.Note this may not be an accurate time span since years and months are normalized from days, and years and months are out of context. To avoid normalizing days into months and years, use the timestamptz subtraction operator.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>age(val: timestamptz) → interval</code></td><td>Calculates the interval between <code>val</code> and the current time, normalized into years, months and days.Note this may not be an accurate time span since years and months are normalized from days, and years and months are out of context. To avoid normalizing days into months and years, use <code>now() - timestamptz</code>.</td><td>Stable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>clock&#95;timestamp() → timestamp</code></td><td>Returns the current system time on one of the cluster nodes.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>clock&#95;timestamp() → timestamptz</code></td><td>Returns the current system time on one of the cluster nodes.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>current&#95;date() → date</code></td><td>Returns the date of the current transaction.The value is based on a timestamp picked when the transaction starts and which stays constant throughout the transaction. This timestamp has no relationship with the commit order of concurrent transactions.</td><td>Stable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>current&#95;timestamp() → date</code></td><td>Returns the time of the current transaction.The value is based on a timestamp picked when the transaction starts and which stays constant throughout the transaction. This timestamp has no relationship with the commit order of concurrent transactions.This function is the preferred overload and will be evaluated by default.</td><td>Stable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>current&#95;timestamp(precision: int) → date</code></td><td>Returns the time of the current transaction.The value is based on a timestamp picked when the transaction starts and which stays constant throughout the transaction. default.</td><td>Stable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>date&#95;part(element: string, input: date) → float</code></td><td>Extracts <code>element</code> from <code>input</code>.Compatible elements: millennium, century, decade, year, isoyear, quarter, month, week, dayofweek, isodow, dayofyear, julian, hour, minute, second, millisecond, microsecond, epoch</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>date&#95;part(element: string, input: interval) → float</code></td><td>Extracts <code>element</code> from <code>input</code>.Compatible elements: millennium, century, decade, year, month, day, hour, minute, second, millisecond, microsecond, epoch</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>date&#95;part(element: string, input: time) → epoch</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>date&#95;part(element: string, input: timestamp) → float</code></td><td>Extracts <code>element</code> from <code>input</code>.Compatible elements: ### ID generation functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>experimental&#95;uuid&#95;v4() → bytes</code></td><td>Returns a UUID.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>gen&#95;random&#95;ulid() → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a random ULID and returns it as a value of UUID type.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>gen&#95;random&#95;uuid() → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a random version 4 UUID, and returns it as a value of UUID type.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>unique&#95;rowid() → int</code></td><td>Returns a unique ID used by CockroachDB to generate unique row IDs if a Primary Key isn’t defined for the table. The value is a combination of the insert timestamp and the ID of the node executing the statement, which guarantees this combination is globally unique. However, there can be gaps and the order is not completely guaranteed.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>unordered&#95;unique&#95;rowid() → int</code></td><td>Returns a unique ID. The value is a combination of the insert timestamp (bit-reversed) and the ID of the node executing the statement, which guarantees this combination is globally unique. The way it is generated is statistically likely to not have any ordering relative to previously generated values.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;generate&#95;v1() → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a version 1 UUID, and returns it as a value of UUID type. To avoid exposing the server’s real MAC address, this uses a random MAC address and a timestamp. Essentially, this is an alias for uuid&#95;generate&#95;v1mc.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;generate&#95;v1mc() → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a version 1 UUID, and returns it as a value of UUID type. This uses a random MAC address and a timestamp.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;generate&#95;v3(namespace: uuid, name: string) → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a version 3 UUID in the given namespace using the specified input name, with md5 as the hashing method. The namespace should be one of the special constants produced by the uuid&#95;ns&#95;&#42;() functions.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;generate&#95;v4() → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a random version 4 UUID, and returns it as a value of UUID type.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;generate&#95;v5(namespace: uuid, name: string) → uuid</code></td><td>Generates a version 5 UUID in the given namespace using the specified input name. This is similar to a version 3 UUID, except it uses SHA-1 for hashing.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;nil() → uuid</code></td><td>Returns a nil UUID constant.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;ns&#95;dns() → uuid</code></td><td>Returns a constant designating the DNS namespace for UUIDs.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;ns&#95;oid() → uuid</code></td><td>Returns a constant designating the ISO object identifier (OID) namespace for UUIDs. These are unrelated to the OID type used internally in the database.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;ns&#95;url() → uuid</code></td><td>Returns a constant designating the URL namespace for UUIDs.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;ns&#95;x500() → uuid</code></td><td>Returns a constant designating the X.500 distinguished name (DN) namespace for UUIDs.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>uuid&#95;v4() → bytes</code></td><td>Returns a UUID.</td><td>Volatile</td></tr></tbody></table>

### INET functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>abbrev(val: inet) → string</code></td><td>Converts the combined IP address and prefix length to an abbreviated display format as text.For INET types, this will omit the prefix length if it’s not the default (32 or IPv4, 128 for IPv6)For example, <code>abbrev('192.168.1.2/24')</code> returns <code>'192.168.1.2/24'</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>broadcast(val: inet) → inet</code></td><td>Gets the broadcast address for the network address represented by the value.For example, <code>broadcast('192.168.1.2/24')</code> returns <code>'192.168.1.255/24'</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>family(val: inet) → int</code></td><td>Extracts the IP family of the value; 4 for IPv4, 6 for IPv6.For example, <code>family('::1')</code> returns <code>6</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>host(val: inet) → string</code></td><td>Extracts the address part of the combined address/prefixlen value as text.For example, <code>host('192.168.1.2/16')</code> returns <code>'192.168.1.2'</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>hostmask(val: inet) → inet</code></td><td>Creates an IP host mask corresponding to the prefix length in the value.For example, <code>hostmask('192.168.1.2/16')</code> returns <code>'0.0.255.255'</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>masklen(val: inet) → int</code></td><td>Retrieves the prefix length stored in the value.For example, <code>masklen('192.168.1.2/16')</code> returns <code>16</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>netmask(val: inet) → inet</code></td><td>Creates an IP network mask corresponding to the prefix length in the value.For example, <code>netmask('192.168.1.2/16')</code> returns <code>'255.255.0.0'</code></td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>set&#95;masklen(val: inet, prefixlen: int) → inet</code></td><td>Sets the prefix length of <code>val</code> to <code>prefixlen</code>.For example, <code>set&#95;masklen('192.168.1.2', 16)</code> returns <code>'192.168.1.2/16'</code>.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr></tbody></table>

### JSONB functions

### STRING[] functions

<table><thead><tr><th>Function → Returns</th><th>Description</th><th>Volatility</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a></a><code>regexp&#95;split&#95;to&#95;array(string: string, pattern: string) → string&#91;&#93;</code></td><td>Split string using a POSIX regular expression as the delimiter.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>regexp&#95;split&#95;to&#95;array(string: string, pattern: string, flags: string) → string&#91;&#93;</code></td><td>Split string using a POSIX regular expression as the delimiter with flags.<br/><br/>CockroachDB supports the following flags:<br/><br/>Flag | Description<br/><br/><strong>c</strong> | Case-sensitive matching<br/><br/><strong>g</strong> | Global matching (match each substring instead of only the first)<br/><br/><strong>i</strong> | Case-insensitive matching<br/><br/><strong>m</strong> or <strong>n</strong> | Newline-sensitive (see below)<br/><br/><strong>p</strong> | Partial newline-sensitive matching (see below)<br/><br/><strong>s</strong> | Newline-insensitive (default)<br/><br/><strong>w</strong> | Inverse partial newline-sensitive matching (see below)<br/><br/>Mode | <code>.</code> and <code>&#91;^...&#93;</code> match newlines | <code>^</code> and <code>&#36;</code> match line boundaries<br/><br/>s | yes | no<br/><br/>w | yes | yes<br/><br/>p | no | no<br/><br/>m/n | no | yes</td><td>Immutable</td></tr></tbody></table>

Returns NULL if the shape is not a Polygon, or the ring does not exist.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>st&#95;intersection(geography&#95;a: geography, geography&#95;b: geography) → geography</code></td><td>Returns the point intersections of the given geographies.This operation is done by transforming the object into a Geometry. This occurs by translating the Geography objects into Geometry objects before applying an LAEA, UTM or Web Mercator based projection based on the bounding boxes of the given Geography objects. When the result is calculated, the result is transformed back into a Geography with SRID 4326.This function utilizes the GEOS module.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>st&#95;intersection(geometry&#95;a: geometry, geometry&#95;b: geometry) → geometry</code></td><td>Returns the point intersections of the given | Description<br/><br/><strong>c</strong> | Case-sensitive matching<br/><br/><strong>g</strong> | Global matching (match each substring instead of only the first)<br/><br/><strong>i</strong> | Case-insensitive matching<br/><br/><strong>m</strong> or <strong>n</strong> | Newline-sensitive (see below)<br/><br/><strong>p</strong> | Partial newline-sensitive matching (see below)<br/><br/><strong>s</strong> | Newline-insensitive (default)<br/><br/><strong>w</strong> | Inverse partial newline-sensitive matching (see below)<br/><br/>Mode | <code>.</code> and <code>&#91;^...&#93;</code> match newlines | <code>^</code> and <code>&#36;</code> match line boundaries<br/><br/>s | yes | no<br/><br/>w | yes | yes<br/><br/>p | no | no<br/><br/>m/n | no | yes</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>repeat(input: string, repeat&#95;counter: int) → string</code></td><td>Concatenates <code>input</code><code>repeat&#95;counter</code> number of <code>return&#95;set</code> characters from <code>input</code>.</td><td>Immutable</td></tr><tr><td><a></a><code>rpad(string: string, length: int) → string</code></td><td>Pads <code>string</code> to ## Aggregate functions

For examples showing how to use aggregate functions, see [the `SELECT` clause documentation](/docs/v25.4/select-clause#aggregate-functions).

<Note>
Non-commutative aggregate functions are sensitive to the order in which the rows are processed in the surrounding [`SELECT` clause](/docs/v25.4/select-clause#aggregate-functions). To specify the order in which input rows are processed, you can add an [`ORDER BY`](/docs/v25.4/order-by) clause within the function argument list. For examples, see the [`SELECT` clause](/docs/v25.4/select-clause#order-aggregate-function-input-rows-by-column) documentation.
</Note>

## Operators

The following table lists all CockroachDB operators from highest to lowest precedence, i.e., the order in which they will be evaluated within a statement. Operators with the same precedence are left associative. This means that those operators are grouped together starting from the left and moving right.

<table><thead><tr><th>Order of Precedence</th><th>Operator</th><th>Name</th><th>Operator Arity</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td><code>.</code></td><td>Member field access operator</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td><code>::</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#explicit-type-coercions">Type cast</a></td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td><code>-</code></td><td>Unary minus</td><td>unary (prefix)</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&#126;</code></td><td>Bitwise not</td><td>unary (prefix)</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td><code>^</code></td><td>Exponentiation</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td><code>&#42;</code></td><td>Multiplication</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>/</code></td><td>Division</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>//</code></td><td>Floor division</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>%</code></td><td>Modulo, or text similarity when accessing a <code>STRING</code> column. For more information, see <a href="/docs/v25.4/trigram-indexes#comparisons">Trigram Indexes</a>.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td><code>+</code></td><td>Addition</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>-</code></td><td>Subtraction</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td><code>&lt;&lt;</code></td><td>Bitwise left-shift</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&gt;&gt;</code></td><td>Bitwise right-shift</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&amp;&amp;</code></td><td>Overlaps</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td><code>&amp;</code></td><td>Bitwise AND</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td><code>#</code></td><td>Bitwise XOR</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td><code>|</code></td><td>Bitwise OR</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td><code>||</code></td><td>Concatenation</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt; ANY</code>, <code>SOME</code>, <code>ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "less than" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&gt; ANY</code>, <code>SOME</code>, <code>ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "greater than" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>= ANY</code>, <code>SOME</code>, <code>ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "equal" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt;= ANY</code>, <code>SOME</code>, <code>ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "less than or equal" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&gt;= ANY</code>, <code>SOME</code>, <code>ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "greater than or equal" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt;&gt; ANY</code> / <code>!= ANY</code>, <code>&lt;&gt; SOME</code> / <code>!= SOME</code>, <code>&lt;&gt; ALL</code> / <code>!= ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a> "not equal" comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&#91;NOT&#93; LIKE ANY</code>, <code>&#91;NOT&#93; LIKE SOME</code>, <code>&#91;NOT&#93; LIKE ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a><code>LIKE</code> comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&#91;NOT&#93; ILIKE ANY</code>, <code>&#91;NOT&#93; ILIKE SOME</code>, <code>&#91;NOT&#93; ILIKE ALL</code></td><td><a href="/docs/v25.4/scalar-expressions#multi-valued-comparisons">Multi-valued</a><code>ILIKE</code> comparison</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>-&gt;</code></td><td>Access a JSONB field, returning a JSONB value.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>-&gt;&gt;</code></td><td>Access a JSONB field, returning a string.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>@&gt;</code></td><td>Tests whether the left JSONB or array field contains the right JSONB or array field.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt;@</code></td><td>Tests whether the left JSONB or array field is contained by the right JSONB or array field.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>#&gt;</code></td><td>Access a JSONB field at the specified path, returning a JSONB value.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>#&gt;&gt;</code></td><td>Access a JSONB field at the specified path, returning a string.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>?</code></td><td>Does the key or element string exist within the JSONB value?</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>?&amp;</code></td><td>Do all the key or element strings exist within the JSONB value?</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>?|</code></td><td>Do any of the key or element strings exist within the JSONB value?</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td><code>&#91;NOT&#93; BETWEEN</code></td><td>Value is &#91;not&#93; within the range specified</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&#91;NOT&#93; BETWEEN SYMMETRIC</code></td><td>Like <code>&#91;NOT&#93; BETWEEN</code>, but in non-sorted order. b)</code>.</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&#91;NOT&#93; IN</code></td><td>Value is &#91;not&#93; in the set of values insensitive</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>!&#126;&#42;</code></td><td>Does not match regular expression, case insensitive</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td><code>=</code></td><td>Equal</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt;</code></td><td>Less than</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&gt;</code></td><td>Greater than</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&lt;=</code></td><td>Less than or equal to</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>&gt;=</code></td><td>Greater than or equal to</td><td>binary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td><code>!=</code>, <code>&lt;&gt;</code></td><td>Not
